## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt in a chemical reaction system. The rate likely follows classical rate law forms where dA/dt depends on concentration A (and possibly explicit time dependence from integrated forms of other species).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Reversible second-order to first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A (mixed order reversible)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-catalyzed reaction with conservation law)
- Second-order with two species (integrated): dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - c2 * A) (bimolecular with stoichiometric constraint)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first and second order)
- Time-dependent forcing with decay: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (coupled species with explicit time solution substituted)
- Competitive inhibition form: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (substrate inhibition kinetics)
- Cubic autocatalysis: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 * (c1 - A) (cubic autocatalytic reaction)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface reaction kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservation of mass in closed systems → rate expressions contain terms like (c - A) representing consumed co-reactant or product concentration
- Elementary reaction mechanisms → rate is a monomial in concentrations with integer exponents matching stoichiometric coefficients
- Equilibrium approach → rate expression is a difference of forward and reverse terms: c0*A^n - c1*A^m with n > m
- Enzyme/surface saturation → rational functions of A with denominator representing binding site competition
- Coupled ODE systems with eliminated variables → explicit time dependence appears through substituted analytical solutions of other species, often as exp(c*t) terms
- Autocatalytic feedback → product terms like A*(c-A) creating logistic-type growth with a carrying capacity set by initial total concentration
- Chain reaction mechanisms → fractional power dependencies A^(1/2) or A^(3/2) arising from quasi-steady-state radical concentrations
- Sequential reactions with intermediate → rate depends on both A and t through terms like t*exp(c*t) representing intermediate species buildup
